# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

# Django URL Patterns Migration from patterns() to list

## Your Task

Find all Python source files in django/django that implement URL routing: the removed patterns() function (pre-1.10), the current urlpatterns list handling, the include() function, and the URL dispatcher that processes both legacy and current URL definitions.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/django--674eda1c.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/django--674eda1c` (django/django)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [

  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Excellent! I've successfully completed a comprehensive analysis of Django's URL routing system and created the answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`. 

## Summary of Findings

I identified **10 key Python files** that implement Django URL routing:

### Core URL Routing Files:
1. **django/urls/conf.py** - Public API for `include()`, `path()`, and `re_path()` functions
2. **django/urls/resolvers.py** - URL dispatcher with `URLPattern`, `URLResolver`, `ResolverMatch` classes and pattern classes (`RegexPattern`, `RoutePattern`, `LocalePrefixPattern`)
3. **django/urls/base.py** - High-level API for `resolve()`, `reverse()`, and URL configuration functions
4. **django/urls/converters.py** - Path converters (IntConverter, StringConverter, etc.)
5. **django/urls/exceptions.py** - Exception classes (`Resolver404`, `NoReverseMatch`)
6. **django/urls/utils.py** - Utility functions like `get_callable()` for loading views
7. **django/urls/__init__.py** - Module exports

### Configuration Files:
8. **django/conf/urls/__init__.py** - Handler error views and backwards-compatible exports
9. **django/conf/urls/i18n.py** - `i18n_patterns()` for internationalized URLs
10. **django/conf/urls/static.py** - Static file serving helper

### Key Findings:

- **Removed patterns() function**: The `django.conf.urls.patterns()` function was removed in Django 1.10. It previously took a prefix argument and returned URL patterns, but modern Django uses direct list syntax with `path()` and `re_path()`

- **URL Resolution Chain**: `include()` → `_path()` → `URLResolver`/`URLPattern` → `get_resolver()` → `resolve()`

- **Flexible Pattern System**: The URL dispatcher handles both legacy regex patterns (`RegexPattern`) and modern simplified patterns (`RoutePattern`), plus special `LocalePrefixPattern` for
... (truncated)

defining URL patterns:\\n\\n- **include()** - Function that allows including URL patterns from other modules or inline URL pattern lists. Returns a tuple of (urlconf_module, app_name, namespace)\\n- **path()** - Creates URL patterns using a simpler, more readable syntax (e.g., `path('articles/<int:year>/', view)`)\\n- **re_path()** - Creates URL patterns using regular expressions (e.g., `re_path(r'^articles/(?P<year>[0-9]{4})/$', view)`)\\n- **_path()** - Internal helper function that both path() and re_path() are based on via functools.partial, handling the common logic for creating URL patterns\\n\\n### URL Dispatcher and Resolution (django/urls/resolvers.py)\\n\\nThis module contains the core URL dispatcher that processes both legacy and current URL definitions:\\n\\n**Pattern Classes:**\\n- **RegexPattern** - Handles regex-based URL patterns with full regex capabilities\\n- **RoutePattern** - Handles simplified path() patterns using angle bracket syntax like `<int:pk>`\\n- **LocalePrefixPattern** - Special pattern for internationalized URLs, used by i18n_patterns()\\n\\n**Main Classes:**\\n- **URLPattern** - Represents a single URL pattern that maps to a view. Contains pattern, callback, default_args, and name\\n- **URLResolver** - Represents a resolver that can contain nested URL patterns. Acts as a container for both URLPattern and nested URLResolver instances\\n- **ResolverMatch** - Returned from successful URL resolution, contains the matched view function, captured arguments, kwargs, url_name, and namespace information\\n\\n**Key Functions:**\\n- **get_resolver()** - Returns a URLResolver instance for the given URLconf, with caching via _get_cached_resolver()\\n- **_route_to_regex()** - Converts simplified path() routes to compiled regular expressions and extracts converters (e.g., `<int:id>` becomes `(?P<id>[0-9]+)`)\\n- **URLResolver.resolve()** - Main URL resolution method that takes a path string and returns a ResolverMatch or raises Resolver404\\n- **URLResolver._populate()** - Populates internal lookup dictionaries for reverse URL resolution and caching\\n\\n### URL Resolution and Reversal (django/urls/base.py)\\n\\nThis module provides the high-level URL resolution and reversal API:\\n\\n- **resolve()** - Takes a URL path and returns a ResolverMatch by calling get_resolver(urlconf).resolve(path)\\n- **reverse()** - Takes a view name and returns the corresponding URL, with support for namespaces, args, kwargs, query parameters, and fragments\\n- **reverse_lazy()** - Lazy version of reverse() for use at module load time\\n- **get_urlconf()** - Returns the currently active URLconf for the current thread/asyncio task\\n- **set_urlconf()** - Sets a custom URLconf for the current thread/asyncio task (useful in tests and middleware)\\n- **is_valid_path()** - Convenience wrapper that returns a ResolverMatch if path resolves, False otherwise\\n- **translate_url()** - Translates URLs between languages using i18n_patterns\\n\\n### URL Converters (django/urls/converters.py)\\n\\nProvides type converters for path() parameters:\\n\\n- **IntConverter** - Matches integers in URLs\\n- **StringConverter** - Matches any string except '/'\\n- **UUIDConverter** - Matches UUID format strings\\n- **SlugConverter** - Matches slug format (letters, numbers, hyphens, underscores)\\n- **PathConverter** - Raised when a URL path cannot be resolved to a view (subclass of Http404)\\n- **NoReverseMatch** - Raised when reverse() cannot find a URL for the given view name\\n\\n### Utilities (django/urls/utils.py)\\n\\n- **get_callable()** - Converts string import paths like 'myapp.views.myview' to actual callable view functions\\n- **get_mod_func()** - Splits a dotted path into module and function name\\n\\n### Internationalization (django/conf/urls/i18n.py)\\n\\n- **i18n_patterns()** - Wraps URL patterns to add language code prefixes (e.g., '/en/', '/fr/')\\n- **is_language_prefix_patterns_used()** - Detects if i18n_patterns is used in the URLconf\\n\\n### Static Files (django/conf/urls/static.py)\\n\\n- **static()** - Prior to 1.10, URL patterns were defined using:\\n\\n```python\\nfrom django.conf.urls import patterns, url\\nurlpatterns = patterns('myapp.views', \\n    url(r'^article/$', 'article_view'),\\n)\\n```\\n\\nModern Django (1.10+) uses direct list syntax with path() and re_path():\\n\\n```python\\nfrom django.urls import path, re_path\\nfrom . import views\\nurlpatterns = [\\n    path('article/', views.article_view),\\n    re_path(r'^regex/(?P<id>[0-9]+)/$', views.view_with_id),\\n]\\n```\\n\\nThe URL dispatcher's URLResolver and URLPattern classes handle both the old string-based view references (via get_callable()) and modern callable/class-based views, providing backwards compatibility during the transition period.\"\n}\n",

defining URL patterns:\\n\\n- **include()** - Function that allows including URL patterns from other modules or inline URL pattern lists. Returns a tuple of (urlconf_module, app_name, namespace)\\n- **path()** - Creates URL patterns using a simpler, more readable syntax (e.g., `path('articles/<int:year>/', view)`)\\n- **re_path()** - Creates URL patterns using regular expressions (e.g., `re_path(r'^articles/(?P<year>[0-9]{4})/$', view)`)\\n- **_path()** - Internal helper function that both path() and re_path() are based on via functools.partial, handling the common logic for creating URL patterns\\n\\n### URL Dispatcher and Resolution (django/urls/resolvers.py)\\n\\nThis module contains the core URL dispatcher that processes both legacy and current URL definitions:\\n\\n**Pattern Classes:**\\n- **RegexPattern** - Handles regex-based URL patterns with full regex capabilities\\n- **RoutePattern** - Handles simplified path() patterns using angle bracket syntax like `<int:pk>`\\n- **LocalePrefixPattern** - Special pattern for internationalized URLs, used by i18n_patterns()\\n\\n**Main Classes:**\\n- **URLPattern** - Represents a single URL pattern that maps to a view. Contains pattern, callback, default_args, and name\\n- **URLResolver** - Represents a resolver that can contain nested URL patterns. Main URL resolution method that takes a path string and returns a ResolverMatch or raises Resolver404\\n- **URLResolver._populate()** - Populates internal lookup dictionaries for reverse URL resolution and caching\\n\\n### URL Resolution and Reversal (django/urls/base.py)\\n\\nThis module provides the high-level URL resolution and reversal API:\\n\\n- **resolve()** - Takes a URL path and returns a ResolverMatch by calling get_resolver(urlconf).resolve(path)\\n- **reverse()** - Takes a view name and returns the corresponding URL, with support for namespaces, args, kwargs, query parameters, and fragments\\n- **reverse_lazy()** - Lazy version of reverse() for use at module load time\\n- **get_urlconf()** - Returns the currently active URLconf for the current thread/asyncio task\\n- **set_urlconf()** - Sets a custom URLconf for the current thread/asyncio task (useful in tests and middleware)\\n- **is_valid_path()** - Convenience wrapper that returns a ResolverMatch if path resolves, False otherwise\\n- **translate_url()** - Translates URLs between languages using i18n_patterns\\n\\n### URL Converters (django/urls/converters.py)\\n\\nProvides type converters for path() parameters:\\n\\n- **IntConverter** - Matches integers in URLs\\n- **StringConverter** - Matches any string except '/'\\n- **UUIDConverter** - Matches UUID format strings\\n- **SlugConverter** - Matches slug format (letters, numbers, hyphens, underscores)\\n- **PathConverter** - Matches any string including '/'\\n- **get_converters()** - Returns dict of all available converters (built-in + registered)\\n- **register_converter()** - Allows applications to register custom converters\\n\\n### Exceptions (django/urls/exceptions.py)\\n\\n- **Resolver404** - Raised when a URL path cannot be resolved to a view (subclass of Http404)\\n- **NoReverseMatch** - Raised when reverse() cannot find a URL for the given view name\\n\\n### Utilities (django/urls/utils.py)\\n\\n- **get_callable()** - Converts string import paths like 'myapp.views.myview' to actual callable view functions\\n- **get_mod_func()** - Splits a dotted path into module and function name\\n\\n### Internationalization (django/conf/urls/i18n.py)\\n\\n- **i18n_patterns()** - Wraps URL patterns to add language code prefixes (e.g., '/en/', '/fr/')\\n- **is_language_prefix_patterns_used()** - Detects if i18n_patterns is used in the URLconf\\n\\n### Static Files (django/conf/urls/static.py)\\n\\n- **static()** - Helper function to serve static files in development mode using a URL pattern\\n\\n### Configuration (django/conf/urls/__init__.py)\\n\\nExports handler error views (handler400, handler403, handler404, handler500) and the include() function for backwards compatibility.\\n\\n### Migration from patterns() to list (Django 1.10)\\n\\nThe **patterns()** function from `django.conf.urls` was removed in Django 1.10. Prior to 1.10, URL patterns were defined using:\\n\\n```python\\nfrom django.conf.urls import patterns, url\\nurlpatterns = patterns('myapp.views', \\n    url(r'^article/$', 'article_view'),\\n)\\n```\\n\\nModern Django (1.10+) uses direct list syntax with path() and re_path():\\n\\n```python\\nfrom django.urls import path, re_path\\nfrom . import views\\nurlpatterns = [\\n    path('article/', views.article_view),\\n    re_path(r'^regex/(?P<id>[0-9]+)/$', views.view_with_id),\\n]\\n```\\n\\nThe URL dispatcher's URLResolver and URLPattern classes handle both the old string-based view references (via get_callable()) and modern callable/class-based views, providing backwards compatibility during the transition period.\"\n}\n",
